Applying an object to a Deltas means to append a Delta\n    64→// except when the potentially appended Delta is a Deleted and the\n    65→// Deltas already ends with a Deleted.  In that case the Deltas does\n    66→// not grow, although the terminal Deleted will be replaced by the new\n    67→// Deleted if the older Deleted's object is a\n    68→// DeletedFinalStateUnknown.\n    69→//\n    70→// The other difference is that DeltaFIFO has two additional ways that\n    71→// an object can be applied to an accumulator: Replaced and Sync.\n    72→// If EmitDeltaTypeReplaced is not set to true, Sync will be used in\n    73→// replace events for backwards compatibility.  Sync is used for periodic\n    74→// resync events.\n    75→//\n    76→// DeltaFIFO is a producer-consumer queue, where a Reflector is\n    77→// intended to be the producer, and the consumer is whatever calls\n    78→// the Pop() method.\n    79→//\n    80→// DeltaFIFO solves this use case:\n    81→//   - You want to process every object change (delta) at most once.\n    82→//   - When you process an object, you want to see everything\n    83→//     that's happened to it since you last processed it.\n    84→//   - You want to process the deletion of some of the objects.\n    85→//   - You might want to periodically reprocess objects.\n    86→//\n    87→// DeltaFIFO's Pop(), Get(), and GetByKey() methods return\n    88→// interface{} to satisfy the Store/Queue interfaces, but they\n    89→// will always return an object of type Deltas. It is used to decide which items are missing\n\t// when Replace() is called; 'Deleted' deltas are produced for the missing items.\n\t// KnownObjects may be nil if you can tolerate missing deletions on Replace().\n\tKnownObjects KeyListerGetter\n\n\t// EmitDeltaTypeReplaced indicates that the queue consumer\n\t// understands the Replaced DeltaType. Applying an object to a Deltas means to append a Delta\n// except when the potentially appended Delta is a Deleted and the\n// Deltas already ends with a Deleted.  In that case the Deltas does\n// not grow, although the terminal Deleted will be replaced by the new\n// Deleted if the older Deleted's object is a\n// DeletedFinalStateUnknown.\n//\n// The other difference is that DeltaFIFO has two additional ways that\n// an object can be applied to an accumulator: Replaced and Sync.\n// If EmitDeltaTypeReplaced is not set to true, Sync will be used in\n// replace events for backwards compatibility. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01Syemxss682pKYHTUACk6mq","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→/*\n     2→Copyright 2015 The Kubernetes Authors.\n     3→\n     4→Licensed under the Apache License, Version 2.0 (the \"License\");\n     5→you may not use this file except in compliance with the License.\n     6→You may obtain a copy of the License at\n     7→\n     8→    http://www.apache.org/licenses/LICENSE-2.0\n     9→\n    10→Unless required by applicable law or agreed to in writing, software\n    11→distributed under the License is distributed on an \"AS IS\" BASIS,\n    12→WITHOUT WARRANTIES OR CONDITIONS OF ANY KIND, either express or implied.\n    13→See the License for the specific language governing permissions and\n    14→limitations under the License.\n    15→*/\n    16→\n    17→package cache\n    18→\n    19→import (\n    20→\t\"errors\"\n    21→\t\"fmt\"\n    22→\t\"sync\"\n    23→\t\"time\"\n    24→\n    25→\t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/api/meta\"\n    26→\t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/runtime\"\n    27→\tutilruntime \"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/runtime\"\n    28→\t\"k8s.io/apimachinery/pkg/util/wait\"\n    29→\t\"k8s.io/client-go/tools/cache/synctrack\"\n    30→\t\"k8s.io/utils/buffer\"\n    31→\t\"k8s.io/utils/clock\"\n    32→\n    33→\t\"k8s.io/klog/v2\"\n    34→\n    35→\tclientgofeaturegate \"k8s.io/client-go/features\"\n    36→)\n    37→\n    38→// SharedInformer provides eventually consistent linkage of its\n    39→// clients to the authoritative state of a given collection of\n    40→// objects.  An object is identified by its API group, kind/resource,\n    41→// namespace (if any), and name; the `ObjectMeta.UID` is not part of\n    42→// an object's ID as far as this contract is concerned.  One\n    43→// SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\n    44→// group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\n    45→// SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\n    46→// applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\n    47→//\n    48→// The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\n    49→// access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\n    50→// An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\n    51→// other appropriate content or (2) \"absent\".\n    52→//\n    53→// A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\n    54→// by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\n    55→// machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\n    56→// the state of each relevant object.  This cache is eventually\n    57→// consistent with the authoritative state.  This means that, unless\n    58→// prevented by persistent communication problems, if ever a\n    59→// particular object ID X is authoritatively associated with a state S\n    60→// then for every SharedInformer I whose collection includes (X, S)\n    61→// eventually either (1) I's cache associates X with S or a later\n    62→// state of X, (2) I is stopped, or (3) the authoritative state\n    63→// service for X terminates.  To be formally complete, we say that the\n    64→// absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\n    65→// selector.\n    66→//\n    67→// For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\n    68→// states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\n    69→// states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\n    70→// might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\n    71→// states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\n    72→// ordering between states seen for different objects.\n    73→//\n    74→// The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\n    75→// during `Run()`.\n    76→//\n    77→// As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\n    78→// unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\n    79→// collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\n    80→// SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\n    81→// collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\n    82→// service ends, or communication problems between the two\n    83→// persistently thwart achievement).\n    84→//\n    85→// As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\n    86→// non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\n    87→// removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\n    88→// removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\n    89→// too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\n    90→// problems persistently thwart the desired result).\n    91→//\n    92→// The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\n    93→// objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\n    94→// Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\n    95→// a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\n    96→// into its constituent parts.\n    97→//\n    98→// Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\n    99→// snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\n   100→// will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\n   101→//\n   102→// A client is identified here by a ResourceEventHandler.  For every\n   103→// update to the SharedInformer's local cache and for every client\n   104→// added before `Run()`, eventually either the SharedInformer is\n   105→// stopped or the client is notified of the update.  A client added\n   106→// after `Run()` starts gets a startup batch of notifications of\n   107→// additions of the objects existing in the cache at the time that\n   108→// client was added; also, for every update to the SharedInformer's\n   109→// local cache after that client was added, eventually either the\n   110→// SharedInformer is stopped or that client is notified of that\n   111→// update.  Client notifications happen after the corresponding cache\n   112→// update and, in the case of a SharedIndexInformer, after the\n   113→// corresponding index updates. An object is identified by its API group, kind/resource,\n// namespace (if any), and name; the `ObjectMeta.UID` is not part of\n// an object's ID as far as this contract is concerned.  One\n// SharedInformer provides linkage to objects of a particular API\n// group and kind/resource.  The linked object collection of a\n// SharedInformer may be further restricted to one namespace (if\n// applicable) and/or by label selector and/or field selector.\n//\n// The authoritative state of an object is what apiservers provide\n// access to, and an object goes through a strict sequence of states.\n// An object state is either (1) present with a ResourceVersion and\n// other appropriate content or (2) \"absent\".\n//\n// A SharedInformer maintains a local cache --- exposed by GetStore(),\n// by GetIndexer() in the case of an indexed informer, and possibly by\n// machinery involved in creating and/or accessing the informer --- of\n// the state of each relevant object.  This cache is eventually\n// consistent with the authoritative state.  This means that, unless\n// prevented by persistent communication problems, if ever a\n// particular object ID X is authoritatively associated with a state S\n// then for every SharedInformer I whose collection includes (X, S)\n// eventually either (1) I's cache associates X with S or a later\n// state of X, (2) I is stopped, or (3) the authoritative state\n// service for X terminates.  To be formally complete, we say that the\n// absent state meets any restriction by label selector or field\n// selector.\n//\n// For a given informer and relevant object ID X, the sequence of\n// states that appears in the informer's cache is a subsequence of the\n// states authoritatively associated with X.  That is, some states\n// might never appear in the cache but ordering among the appearing\n// states is correct.  Note, however, that there is no promise about\n// ordering between states seen for different objects.\n//\n// The local cache starts out empty, and gets populated and updated\n// during `Run()`.\n//\n// As a simple example, if a collection of objects is henceforth\n// unchanging, a SharedInformer is created that links to that\n// collection, and that SharedInformer is `Run()` then that\n// SharedInformer's cache eventually holds an exact copy of that\n// collection (unless it is stopped too soon, the authoritative state\n// service ends, or communication problems between the two\n// persistently thwart achievement).\n//\n// As another simple example, if the local cache ever holds a\n// non-absent state for some object ID and the object is eventually\n// removed from the authoritative state then eventually the object is\n// removed from the local cache (unless the SharedInformer is stopped\n// too soon, the authoritative state service ends, or communication\n// problems persistently thwart the desired result).\n//\n// The keys in the Store are of the form namespace/name for namespaced\n// objects, and are simply the name for non-namespaced objects.\n// Clients can use `MetaNamespaceKeyFunc(obj)` to extract the key for\n// a given object, and `SplitMetaNamespaceKey(key)` to split a key\n// into its constituent parts.\n//\n// Every query against the local cache is answered entirely from one\n// snapshot of the cache's state.  Thus, the result of a `List` call\n// will not contain two entries with the same namespace and name.\n//\n// A client is identified here by a ResourceEventHandler.  For every\n// update to the SharedInformer's local cache and for every client\n// added before `Run()`, eventually either the SharedInformer is\n// stopped or the client is notified of the update.  A client added\n// after `Run()` starts gets a startup batch of notifications of\n// additions of the objects existing in the cache at the time that\n// client was added; also, for every update to the SharedInformer's\n// local cache after that client was added, eventually either the\n// SharedInformer is stopped or that client is notified of that\n// update.  Client notifications happen after the corresponding cache\n// update and, in the case of a SharedIndexInformer, after the\n// corresponding index updates.  It is possible that additional cache\n// and index updates happen before such a prescribed notification.\n// For a given SharedInformer and client, the notifications are\n// delivered sequentially.  For a given SharedInformer, client, and\n// object ID, the notifications are delivered in order.  Because\n// `ObjectMeta.UID` has no role in identifying objects, it is possible\n// that when (1) object O1 with ID (e.g. namespace and name) X and\n// `ObjectMeta.UID` U1 in the SharedInformer's local cache is deleted\n// and later (2) another object O2 with ID X and ObjectMeta.UID U2 is\n// created the informer's clients are not notified of (1) and (2) but\n// rather are notified only of an update from O1 to O2. Clients that\n// need to detect such cases might do so by comparing the `ObjectMeta.UID`\n// field of the old and the new object in the code that handles update\n// notifications (i.e. `OnUpdate` method of ResourceEventHandler).\n//\n// A client must process each notification promptly; a SharedInformer\n// is not engineered to deal well with a large backlog of\n// notifications to deliver.  Lengthy processing should be passed off\n// to something else, for example through a\n// `client-go/util/workqueue`.\n//\n// A delete notification exposes the last locally known non-absent\n// state, except that its ResourceVersion is replaced with a\n// ResourceVersion in which the object is actually absent.\ntype SharedInformer interface {\n\t// AddEventHandler adds an event handler to the shared informer using\n\t// the shared informer's resync period.  Events to a single handler are\n\t// delivered sequentially, but there is no coordination between\n\t// different handlers.\n\t// It returns a registration handle for the handler that can be used to\n\t// remove the handler again, or to tell if the handler is synced (has\n\t// seen every item in the initial list).\n\tAddEventHandler(handler ResourceEventHandler) (ResourceEventHandlerRegistration, error)\n\t// AddEventHandlerWithResyncPeriod adds an event handler to the\n\t// shared informer with the requested resync period; zero means\n\t// this handler does not care about resyncs.  The resync operation\n\t// consists of delivering to the handler an update notification\n\t// for every object in the informer's local cache; it does not add","numLines":150,"startLine":1,"totalLines":1019}}}

DeltaFIFO Queue (delta_fifo.go)**: A producer-consumer queue that accumulates deltas for each object. The DeltaFIFO struct (line 101) stores changes as Deltas (a slice of Delta objects), where each Delta contains a DeltaType (Added, Updated, Deleted, Replaced, Sync) and the object state. This queue acts as the intermediate buffer between the Reflector and the Controller.\\n\\n**4. Controller (controller.go)**: The controller.processLoop() method (line 193) continuously pops Deltas from the DeltaFIFO queue. This method sends each notification to all registered listeners by calling listener.add(), filtering based on sync vs. non-sync notifications according to each listener's resync requirements.\\n\\n**8. ProcessorListener (shared_informer.go:869)**: Each listener has:\\n   - addCh: Channel receiving notifications from the processor\\n   - nextCh: Channel delivering notifications to the handler goroutine\\n   - pendingNotifications: Ring buffer holding notifications waiting to be dispatched\\n   - The pop() method (line 936) runs in a separate goroutine, dequeuing from addCh and buffering in pendingNotifications, then sending to nextCh\\n   - The run() method (line 966) runs in another goroutine, receiving from nextCh and invoking the handler's OnAdd, OnUpdate, or OnDelete methods\\n\\n**9. ListWatch.WatchFunc initiates a watch connection to the API server and returns a watch.Interface for streaming events.\\n\\n**2. Reflector (reflector.go)**: The primary watcher component that maintains synchronization between the API server and local cache. The Reflector.ListAndWatch() method (line 348) orchestrates the initial list and subsequent watch operations. The handleAnyWatch() function (line 782) processes individual watch events (Added, Modified, Deleted) received from the API server and calls store.Add(), store.Update(), or store.Delete() to update the DeltaFIFO queue.\\n\\n**3. DeltaFIFO Queue (delta_fifo.go)**: A producer-consumer queue that accumulates deltas for each object. The DeltaFIFO struct (line 101) stores changes as Deltas (a slice of Delta objects), where each Delta contains a DeltaType (Added, Updated, Deleted, Replaced, Sync) and the object state. This queue acts as the intermediate buffer between the Reflector and the Controller.\\n\\n**4. Controller (controller.go)**: The controller.processLoop() method (line 193) continuously pops Deltas from the DeltaFIFO queue. Each Pop operation invokes the Process function (which is sharedIndexInformer.HandleDeltas) with the dequeued Deltas and an isInInitialList flag.\\n\\n**5. The processDeltas() function iterates through each Delta and updates the local indexer (cache.Store), then invokes the appropriate handler method (OnAdd, OnUpdate, or OnDelete) through the ResourceEventHandler interface.\\n\\n**6.
